# Repository Instructions

## Execution Workflow
- Treat `references/plan.md` as the authoritative implementation plan.
- Always start with the earliest unfinished plan item.
- Break that item into concrete tasks, complete them one at a time, verify each one, and only then move to the next task.
- Update `references/plan.md` only when implementation reality requires a change.

## Remote Sync
- After completing a substantial plan item such as `0.2`, `0.3`, `1.1`, or `3.2`, create a focused commit and push it to `origin` so the remote repository reflects major progress checkpoints.

## Phase Checkpoints
- When an entire phase is complete, create a clearly named GitHub checkpoint for that phase so there is a stable recovery marker for later reference.
- Prefer a GitHub milestone for tracking visibility, and use a git-native checkpoint such as a tag or equivalent marker when an actual rollback point is required.
- Use rollback tags in the format `rollback/phase-<n>-<short-name>` so phase checkpoints are easy to identify and reuse.

</INSTRUCTIONS>

### 40. Assistant

Option 1, in concrete terms:

`Seed defaults` means:
- the app keeps using the normal shared-item collection it already has
- on a fresh/local save, it checks whether the 5 requested starter items exist
- if they do not exist, it creates them once
- after that, they are normal items:
  - visible in `Items List`
  - editable in `Item Editting`
  - deletable
  - assignable to characters
- existing saves are not overwritten
- the app avoids duplicate starter copies by checking first

So this is not a fixed hardcoded catalog. It is just a one-time default population of normal editable items.

One important scope choice remains:
- current runtime already applies stat/skill/resistance/combat bonuses from items
- current runtime does not yet apply item `power` / `spell` bonus fields mechanically

I need you to lock those two decisions.

### 48. Assistant

<proposed_plan>
## DM Item Management and Starter Items

### Summary
- First implementation step: revert the unintended edit in `project_tracking/tasks_todo.md`.
- Add a new `Item Management` block to the DM Dashboard with two links inside it:
  - `Item Editting`
  - `Items List`
- Add two guarded DM routes:
  - `/dm/items/edit`
  - `/dm/items`
- Create the 5 requested items as normal editable shared items, seeded once per local save:
  - `Bow`
  - `One-Handed Sword`
  - `Two-Handed Sword`
  - `Shield`
  - `Armor`
- Keep the new pages focused on shared-item authoring and browsing. Character assignment/equip stays on character sheets in this slice.

### Key Changes
- **DM navigation and pages**
  - Extend the current DM dashboard card grid with a fourth `Item Management` card using the same visual pattern as the existing three blocks.
  - Put both action buttons directly inside that card so step `5` is satisfied from the dashboard itself.
  - Build `Items List` as a browse page in the current `flow-page` / `flow-card-wide` style.
  - Build `Item Editting` as a detailed single-item editor page, using a sheet-style layout: item picker/list on the left, detailed editor on the right, plus `Create New Item`, `Delete Item`, and navigation actions.

- **Starter item bootstrap**
  - Seed the 5 starter items once during persisted-state bootstrap, not on every render.
  - Add a persisted bootstrap flag, e.g. `starterItemsInitialized`, to the local storage envelope so starter items are not recreated after deletion.
  - Use fixed starter item ids so tests and page routing can target them deterministically.
  - Defaults:
    - `Bow` -> existing `weapon:bow`
    - `One-Handed Sword` -> existing `weapon:one_handed`
    - `Two-Handed Sword` -> existing `weapon:two_handed`
    - `Shield` -> new explicit shield blueprint
    - `Armor` -> existing `armor:light`

- **Item model/editor scope**
  - Add explicit shield support to the shared item model with a dedicated blueprint, rather than pretending shield is generic armor in the UI.
  - Keep the current item runtime behavior for character-sheet fields:
    - stats
    - skills
    - derived combat/resource fields
    - resistances
    - utility traits / notes
  - Extend `BonusProfile` with `spellBonuses: Record<string, number>` so the editor can store selected-spell bonuses separately from selected-power bonuses.
  - Keep `powerBonuses` and new `spellBonuses` as editor-visible and persisted data in this task only; do not add gameplay/runtime application yet.

- **Page design**
  - `Items List`
    - Show all shared items, including the 5 starter items.
    - Each row/card shows: name, blueprint/type, quality, item level, base visible stats, summarized character-sheet impacts, summarized power bonuses, summarized spell bonuses, and an `Edit` action.
    - Include a `Create New Item` button that routes to `Item Editting`.
  - `Item Editting`
    - Optimize for editing one item in detail.
    - Sections should mirror the actual game surfaces already present in the repo:
      - Item identity/base template
      - Character-sheet effects
        - stat bonuses
        - skill bonuses
        - derived bonuses
        - resistance bonuses
        - utility traits / notes
      - Power effects
      - Spell effects
    - Power option values come from the existing power library.
    - Spell option values come from the current spell metadata already used by the cast/casting system, not from a new ad-hoc hardcoded list.
    - Use the auction-house reference only as vocabulary/design guidance; do not add pricing/stock/bid schema in this task.

### Interfaces / Type Changes
- Add routes for `/dm/items` and `/dm/items/edit`.
- Extend persisted storage envelope/state bootstrap logic with `starterItemsInitialized`.
- Extend item typings with:
  - a shield blueprint id
  - `spellBonuses` on `BonusProfile`
- Add item-editor helper data for power/spell option lists based on current repo sources of truth.

### Test Plan
- **Persistence/bootstrap**
  - Starter items are created on first bootstrap only.
  - Starter items are not duplicated on repeated hydrations.
  - After bootstrap is marked complete, deleting a starter item does not cause it to come back automatically on reload.
- **Item model/runtime**
  - Shield blueprint resolves its base bonuses correctly when equipped in a normal non-weapon equipment slot.
  - Existing weapon attack behavior remains unchanged for bow / one-handed / two-handed items.
  - `spellBonuses` and `powerBonuses` serialize, hydrate, and display correctly.
- **DM flow**
  - DM dashboard renders the new `Item Management` block and both links.
  - `Items List` opens from the dashboard and shows the 5 starter items.
  - `Item Editting` opens from the dashboard and from an item edit action in the list.
  - Creating, editing, and deleting an item updates the shared item collection and persists after reload.
- **Non-regression**
  - Existing character-sheet item effects on stats/skills/derived/resistances still work.
  - No new runtime effect is introduced for power/spell bonuses in this slice.

### Assumptions and Defaults
- Revert of the unintended `tasks_todo.md` change happens first.
- UI label stays exactly `Item Editting` to match your requested wording.
- `Armor` defaults to light armor.
- `Shield` defaults to a light shield profile.
- DM item pages are authoring/browsing pages only; ownership, carrying, active state, and equipment assignment remain managed from character sheets for now.
</proposed_plan>

    - resistances
    - utility traits / notes
  - Extend `BonusProfile` with `spellBonuses: Record<string, number>` so the editor can store selected-spell bonuses separately from selected-power bonuses.
  - Keep `powerBonuses` and new `spellBonuses` as editor-visible and persisted data in this task only; do not add gameplay/runtime application yet.

- **Page design**
  - `Items List`
    - Show all shared items, including the 5 starter items.
    - Each row/card shows: name, blueprint/type, quality, item level, base visible stats, summarized character-sheet impacts, summarized power bonuses, summarized spell bonuses, and an `Edit` action.
    - Include a `Create New Item` button that routes to `Item Editting`.
  - `Item Editting`
    - Optimize for editing one item in detail.
    - Sections should mirror the actual game surfaces already present in the repo:
      - Item identity/base template
      - Character-sheet effects
        - stat bonuses
        - skill bonuses
        - derived bonuses
        - resistance bonuses
        - utility traits / notes
      - Power effects
      - Spell effects
    - Power option values come from the existing power library.
    - Spell option values come from the current spell metadata already used by the cast/casting system, not from a new ad-hoc hardcoded list.
    - Use the auction-house reference only as vocabulary/design guidance; do not add pricing/stock/bid schema in this task.

### Interfaces / Type Changes
- Add routes for `/dm/items` and `/dm/items/edit`.
- Extend persisted storage envelope/state bootstrap logic with `starterItemsInitialized`.
- Extend item typings with:
  - a shield blueprint id
  - `spellBonuses` on `BonusProfile`
- Add item-editor helper data for power/spell option lists based on current repo sources of truth.

### Test Plan
- **Persistence/bootstrap**
  - Starter items are created on first bootstrap only.
  - Starter items are not duplicated on repeated hydrations.
  - After bootstrap is marked complete, deleting a starter item does not cause it to come back automatically on reload.
- **Item model/runtime**
  - Shield blueprint resolves its base bonuses correctly when equipped in a normal non-weapon equipment slot.
  - Existing weapon attack behavior remains unchanged for bow / one-handed / two-handed items.
  - `spellBonuses` and `powerBonuses` serialize, hydrate, and display correctly.
- **DM flow**
  - DM dashboard renders the new `Item Management` block and both links.
  - `Items List` opens from the dashboard and shows the 5 starter items.
  - `Item Editting` opens from the dashboard and from an item edit action in the list.
  - Creating, editing, and deleting an item updates the shared item collection and persists after reload.
- **Non-regression**
  - Existing character-sheet item effects on stats/skills/derived/resistances still work.
  - No new runtime effect is introduced for power/spell bonuses in this slice.

### Assumptions and Defaults
- Revert of the unintended `tasks_todo.md` change happens first.
- UI label stays exactly `Item Editting` to match your requested wording.
- `Armor` defaults to light armor.
- `Shield` defaults to a light shield profile.
- DM item pages are authoring/browsing pages only; ownership, carrying, active state, and equipment assignment remain managed from character sheets for now.

### 81. Assistant

From the existing repo plus the authoritative item rules.

Primary code sources:
- [src/types/items.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\types\items.ts)
- [src/lib/items.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\items.ts)

Authoritative rules source:
- [item_rules_v2.1.txt](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\references\originals\item_rules_v2.1.txt)

What was already in the code before my change:
- `weapon:brawl`
- `weapon:one_handed`
- `weapon:two_handed`
- `weapon:oversized`
- `weapon:bow`
- `armor:light`
- `armor:heavy`
- `jewel:jewel`
- `mystic:mystic`

What I added:
- `armor:shield`

Why I added `armor:shield`:
- The rules explicitly separate armor and shields:
  - light shields: `DR +1`
  - heavy shields: `DR +2`
- The existing code had no real shield blueprint, and the old inference path treated `shield` like light armor, which was wrong for the DM item pages you asked for.

So the blueprints were not invented from scratch. Most came from the existing item model, and `shield` was added to align the code with the authoritative rules.

<proposed_plan>
# Item Blueprint/Instance Refactor, Rule Sync, and DM Management

## Summary
- Update [C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\project_tracking\new_thread_context.md](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\project_tracking\new_thread_context.md) first:
  - merge current `## 1` and `## 2` into the new compacted `## 1`
  - write this thread’s compacted context into new `## 2`
  - keep `## 3` in place for now
- Promote [C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\references\originals\item_rules_v2.1.txt](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\references\originals\item_rules_v2.1.txt) to `v2.2`, align the older contradictory prose to section `5`, and update repo references to the new filename.
- Replace the current “shared item only” model with two persisted collections:
  - persisted `itemBlueprints`
  - persisted `itemInstances`
- Keep DM `Item Management`, but expand it to three links:
  - `Item Editting`
  - `Items List`
  - `Blueprint Management`
- Convert the current 5 starter records into starter item instances backed by real blueprints.

## Key Changes
- **Authoritative blueprint catalog**
  - Build the catalog from the rule classifications in section `5`, not from example names.
  - Add blueprint ids for:
    - `weapon:unarmed`
    - `weapon:brawl`
    - `weapon:one_handed`
    - `weapon:two_handed`
    - `weapon:oversized`
    - `weapon:ranged_light`
    - `weapon:pistol`
    - `weapon:bow_long`
    - `weapon:rifle`
    - `weapon:crossbow_heavy`
    - `weapon:shotgun`
    - `weapon:chaingun`
    - `weapon:rocket_launcher`
    - `armor:clothing`
    - `armor:light`
    - `armor:medium`
    - `armor:heavy`
    - `armor:shield_light`
    - `armor:shield_heavy`
    - `mystic:focus`
  - Keep legacy `jewel:jewel` readable for save compatibility, but treat it as legacy until rules define a real jewel baseline.
  - Treat `3-Handed Weapon` as the label for the `oversized` class while still using `handsRequired = 2`.

- **Data model and persistence**
  - Add persisted `ItemBlueprintRecord` with:
    - `id`, `category`, `subtype`, `label`, `defaultName`
    - base combat/spec metadata
    - base stat/skill/derived/resistance profile
    - base visible notes / requirements / traits
    - `overrideItemIds` as the exception list the DM can inspect
  - Change item records into true instances with:
    - `id`, `blueprintId`, `name`, `itemLevel`, `qualityTier`
    - `baseOverrides`
    - `bonusProfile`
    - `knowledge`
    - `assignedCharacterId`
  - Resolve instance mechanics as: `blueprint base` + `instance baseOverrides` + `instance bonusProfile`.
  - Hydration must migrate old item saves into the new blueprint/instance structure and preserve local-save compatibility.

- **Rule sync and runtime**
  - Section `5` wins whenever the old document prose contradicts it.
  - Update the combat/item runtime so physical attack profiles recognize the expanded weapon blueprint set.
  - Store range and AoE metadata on blueprints, but do not implement encounter range or rocket AoE targeting in this pass.
  - Fix current code mismatches to the authoritative rules, including:
    - one-handed melee baseline
    - brawl vs brawl-weapon split
    - armor initiative / stealth / DR baselines
    - light vs heavy shield split
    - occult focus baseline
  - Keep power and spell bonuses persisted and editable, but still non-runtime for now.

- **DM UI**
  - Keep routes:
    - `/dm/items`
    - `/dm/items/edit`
  - Add:
    - `/dm/items/blueprints`
  - `Items List` becomes a line list with expandable rows, not cards.
  - Each expanded item row shows resolved blueprint class, base values, bonus values, assignment controls, power/spell summaries, and edit/open actions.
  - Assignment in `Items List` is single-instance to single-character:
    - assign sets `assignedCharacterId`
    - syncs the character’s owned/inventory links
    - does not auto-equip or auto-activate
    - reassign removes links from the previous character first
  - `Item Editting` shows paired fields for numeric effect families:
    - base field from blueprint or override
    - bonus field from instance bonus profile
  - Base fields are disabled and greyed out by default.
  - `Update Base Specs` enables base editing for the selected item and reveals `Save`.
  - `Save` must branch into:
    - `Update Blueprint Base Values`
    - `Update Base Values Of Only This Item`
  - `Update Base Values Of Only This Item` writes `baseOverrides` and adds the item id to the blueprint’s `overrideItemIds`.
  - If an override no longer differs from blueprint base values, remove that item id from the exception list.
  - `Blueprint Management` is a list/editor page for create/edit/delete blueprints and must expose the blueprint’s exception-item list with links back to those items.

## Test Plan
- Hydration migrates old item saves into blueprint + instance storage without duplicating starter data.

## Key Changes
- **Authoritative blueprint catalog**
  - Build the catalog from the rule classifications in section `5`, not from example names.
  - Add blueprint ids for:
    - `weapon:unarmed`
    - `weapon:brawl`
    - `weapon:one_handed`
    - `weapon:two_handed`
    - `weapon:oversized`
    - `weapon:ranged_light`
    - `weapon:pistol`
    - `weapon:bow_long`
    - `weapon:rifle`
    - `weapon:crossbow_heavy`
    - `weapon:shotgun`
    - `weapon:chaingun`
    - `weapon:rocket_launcher`
    - `armor:clothing`
    - `armor:light`
    - `armor:medium`
    - `armor:heavy`
    - `armor:shield_light`
    - `armor:shield_heavy`
    - `mystic:focus`
  - Keep legacy `jewel:jewel` readable for save compatibility, but treat it as legacy until rules define a real jewel baseline.
  - Treat `3-Handed Weapon` as the label for the `oversized` class while still using `handsRequired = 2`.

- **Data model and persistence**
  - Add persisted `ItemBlueprintRecord` with:
    - `id`, `category`, `subtype`, `label`, `defaultName`
    - base combat/spec metadata
    - base stat/skill/derived/resistance profile
    - base visible notes / requirements / traits
    - `overrideItemIds` as the exception list the DM can inspect
  - Change item records into true instances with:
    - `id`, `blueprintId`, `name`, `itemLevel`, `qualityTier`
    - `baseOverrides`
    - `bonusProfile`
    - `knowledge`
    - `assignedCharacterId`
  - Resolve instance mechanics as: `blueprint base` + `instance baseOverrides` + `instance bonusProfile`.
  - Hydration must migrate old item saves into the new blueprint/instance structure and preserve local-save compatibility.

- **Rule sync and runtime**
  - Section `5` wins whenever the old document prose contradicts it.
  - Update the combat/item runtime so physical attack profiles recognize the expanded weapon blueprint set.
  - Store range and AoE metadata on blueprints, but do not implement encounter range or rocket AoE targeting in this pass.
  - Fix current code mismatches to the authoritative rules, including:
    - one-handed melee baseline
    - brawl vs brawl-weapon split
    - armor initiative / stealth / DR baselines
    - light vs heavy shield split
    - occult focus baseline
  - Keep power and spell bonuses persisted and editable, but still non-runtime for now.

- **DM UI**
  - Keep routes:
    - `/dm/items`
    - `/dm/items/edit`
  - Add:
    - `/dm/items/blueprints`
  - `Items List` becomes a line list with expandable rows, not cards.
  - Each expanded item row shows resolved blueprint class, base values, bonus values, assignment controls, power/spell summaries, and edit/open actions.
  - Assignment in `Items List` is single-instance to single-character:
    - assign sets `assignedCharacterId`
    - syncs the character’s owned/inventory links
    - does not auto-equip or auto-activate
    - reassign removes links from the previous character first
  - `Item Editting` shows paired fields for numeric effect families:
    - base field from blueprint or override
    - bonus field from instance bonus profile
  - Base fields are disabled and greyed out by default.
  - `Update Base Specs` enables base editing for the selected item and reveals `Save`.
  - `Save` must branch into:
    - `Update Blueprint Base Values`
    - `Update Base Values Of Only This Item`
  - `Update Base Values Of Only This Item` writes `baseOverrides` and adds the item id to the blueprint’s `overrideItemIds`.
  - If an override no longer differs from blueprint base values, remove that item id from the exception list.
  - `Blueprint Management` is a list/editor page for create/edit/delete blueprints and must expose the blueprint’s exception-item list with links back to those items.

### 176. User

# Context from my IDE setup:

## Active file: references/originals/item_rules_v2.3.txt

## Open tabs:
- item_rules_v2.3.txt: references/originals/item_rules_v2.3.txt
- item_rules_v2.2.txt: references/originals/item_rules_v2.2.txt
- new_thread_context.md: project_tracking/new_thread_context.md
- power_spell_ingestion_normalized_current.json: references/power_spell_ingestion_normalized_current.json
- item_rules_v2.1.txt: references/originals/item_rules_v2.1.txt

## My request for Codex:
i just realized a logical fallacy. as armors gets lighter, its intiative bonus increases, and clothing having the highest intiative. yet, if a character is not wearing any armor (aka naked), has no initiative bonus. i think that is a logical fallacy. to fix this i think we should give a character +3 initiative. moreover, we should assume all characters would have an outfit put on, thus, we should create a new blueprint: `outfit` and that should provide the same benefits of `Armor / Clothing Or Robes`, and on top of that, all characters should come with an outfit on (along with the benefits). one caveat here is the monsters/mobs. some mobs might not have any clothing on (and for some even not a weapon), which is normal. assume that there will be a direwolf encounter and that mob will not have any clothing on. yet again, we can consider a warhorse that is equipped with protective armor as well. so that brings us to a contradictory situation. i guess i should add in my original plan, i am treating everything as a character including mobs or animals, or anything. 

I want to discuss that with you for a soluiton.

### 177. Assistant

Recommended solution:

1. Do not give `+3 initiative` to every character globally.
2. Split the concept into:
- `unarmored humanoid baseline`
- `default outfit`
- `actual armor`

That removes the contradiction cleanly.

**Why**
- If every character gets `+3`, then direwolves, blobs, undead masses, and other non-humanoids also get it by default, which is not what you want.
- The real distinction is not `character vs not character`; it is `humanoid apparel logic vs non-humanoid body logic`.

**Model I recommend**
- Add a new blueprint: `outfit`
- `outfit` should be the current `Clothing / Robes` equivalent:
  - `initiative +2`
  - `DR +0`
  - chest slot
- Add a separate humanoid unarmored rule:
  - if a humanoid has nothing in the chest slot, they get `+3 initiative`
- Humanoid characters start with an `outfit` equipped by default.
- Non-humanoids do not.
- Armor replaces outfit in the same chest slot, so it does not stack.

That gives you:
- naked humanoid: `+3`
- outfit/clothes: `+2`
- light armor: `+1`
- medium armor: `0` or current medium profile
- heavy armor: `-1`

That progression is logically clean.

**How to handle mobs/animals**
Add a per-character/template flag, something like:
- `apparelMode: humanoid | none`

Behavior:
- `humanoid`
  - starts with default `outfit`
  - gets naked `+3` only if chest slot is empty
- `none`
  - no default outfit
  - no naked-apparel bonus
  - can still wear armor if explicitly assigned

Examples:
- player character: `humanoid`
- city guard: `humanoid`
- direwolf: `none`
- warhorse: `none`, but can still equip armor item

**What I would not do**
- I would not make `outfit` and also give all characters a permanent flat `+3`.
That mixes two different systems and will create balancing confusion.

**Small compatibility note**
- We can keep current blueprint data mostly intact and just rename/alias:
  - current `armor:clothing` -> new displayed blueprint `outfit`
- Or make a real new `outfit` blueprint and retire `armor:clothing`.

My recommendation:
- keep one chest-slot starter blueprint for humanoids
- add humanoid-only naked baseline `+3`
- add `apparelMode` to distinguish humanoids from beasts

If you want, I can next turn this into a precise implementation plan without coding yet.

### 183. Assistant

### 184. Assistant

My recommendation on `robes`:

- Keep `robes` under `clothing`, not `light armor`.
- Do not create a separate mundane `robe` blueprint right now.

Why:
- If `robe` is its own mundane blueprint, it needs a clear 0-PP identity.
- `+1 AC` makes it feel like weak armor.
- `+1 mana` or occult bonuses stop being a mundane baseline and start becoming magical/specialized gear.
- That makes mundane robes mechanically awkward.

Cleaner model:
- `clothing` remains the mundane baseline.
- `robe` is a visual/style variant of clothing, not a separate baseline blueprint.
- Special robes become item instances or magical blueprints built on top of clothing with paid bonuses:
  - mana
  - occultism
  - spell bonus
  - utility traits

So:
- mundane robe = clothing
- magical robe = clothing + explicit bonuses

I think that is the cleanest answer.

For the mobs/animals point:
- I agree with recording it for future character/encounter creation rather than forcing it into the current item pass.
- I added the note/TODO in:
  - [tasks_todo.md](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\project_tracking\tasks_todo.md)
  - [current_notes.md](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\references\current_notes.md)

What I recorded:
- humanoids can use default clothing and naked-state rules
- beasts/mobs can intentionally have no clothing baseline
- both can still equip armor/weapons explicitly

If you want, next we can decide the exact naked/clothing progression numerically before any implementation:
- naked humanoid `+3 init`
- clothing/robe `+2 init`
- light armor `+1 init`
- medium armor `0 init`
- heavy armor `-1 init`

### 265. Assistant

### 266. Assistant

I confirmed it: in the current code, `itemLevel` is mostly the mechanical abstraction, and `qualityTier` is the human-facing label. I’m pulling the exact mapping so the answer is precise.

### 267. Assistant

In this repo, they are not the same thing.

- `qualityTier`:
  - the item’s named rarity/quality label
  - examples: `Common`, `Rare`, `Epic`, `Legendary`
  - the authoritative meaning comes from the PP budget tiers in [item_rules_v2.3.txt](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\references\originals\item_rules_v2.3.txt)
  - this is the design-facing classification

- `itemLevel`:
  - a simplified numeric gate used by the code
  - right now its main gameplay use is item identification:
    - `Artifact Appraisal` can identify an item if `artifactAppraisalLevel >= item.itemLevel`
  - see [items.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\items.ts)

Current code mapping:
- `Common` or unspecified -> `1`
- `Rare` -> `2`
- `Epic` -> `3`
- `Legendary` -> `4`
- `Mythical / Celestial / Demonic` -> `5`

So the practical answer is:
- `qualityTier` = label/rank by PP budget
- `itemLevel` = numeric abstraction the code uses, mainly for appraisal gating

If you want, next I can propose a cleaner model so `itemLevel` is either removed, renamed, or made fully derived from `qualityTier`.

### 268. Assistant

## My request for Codex:
it seems you complicated things unnecessarily. we have item property points (pp) and item tiers. pp of an item decides an item's tier. it has a math. section 2 and 3 and 4 in [item_rules_v2.3.txt](references/originals/item_rules_v2.3.txt) explains this math. 2 and 3 explains pp and 4 explains the relation between pp and item tiers. i think it is unnecssary to create an item level concept whilst we have pp. 

let' s focus on that. as i've told you [item_rules_v2.3.txt](references/originals/item_rules_v2.3.txt) is the authoritative source.

replace item level with pp.
derive pp from active bonuses on the item. math of pp calculation is given in the file. section 2 and 3.

then reflect that pp value to the item tier. hence those two fields should be greyed out autocalculated fields.

```
Item Quality Tiers and PP Budget Capacities:
-	Common: 0 PP (Standard mundane items; base stats only)
-	Uncommon / Masterwork: 1 to 4 PP (Minor enhancements or master-crafted gear)
-	Rare: 5 to 10 PP (Elite gear; typically introduces core stat bonuses)
-	Epic: 11 to 18 PP (Immensely powerful gear; introduces resistances and major effects)
-	Legendary: 19 to 30 PP (Relics of myth with extreme combat impact)
-	Mythical / Celestial / Demonic: 31 to 60+ PP (Reality-bending items that define character builds)
-	Artifact: 1 to 4 PP Base (Starts equivalent to Uncommon. Scales indefinitely by fulfilling specific
```

the biggest issue, i'd assume would be the implementation of the 2.4.'s math to pp. because of `-	Bundle: +1 to All Stats (discounted flat cost for global stat increase): 12 PP `. i guess the easiest way to deal with that is adding an additional field for that. alternatively, you may allow me to add (by adding that UI functionality) new fields, along with their PP costs, hence if I create an item with a bundle effect, i can put it's PP cost into it's PP cost field and that would reflect to the total PP of the item automatically. the problem with that is, assigning the values to the character sheet. I guess, if you would add an option (like in our dice roll popover window) where i can select to what character sheet fields that the newly defined budle effect will relate to and by how much, that would resolve that problem as well. for instance, 
- if i hit add a new property button, 
- and that gives me two fields: select CS fields (as a button) for 1 level and PP cost as a numeric field that would,
- then if i select, let's say, 3 different resistance field through the CS fields popover button,
- and then entering, let's say 8 to the PP cost field,
- and that pp cost field of the new property reflecting to the total property point cost of the item,
- while the selected CS fields (resistances) resistance level increasing 1 level,
we could solve the bundling problem and that would give even more flexibility to the dm to tinker other things.

i want to add these to the document:
```
- Bundle: +1 to All skills (discounted flat cost for global skill increase): 8 PP ,
- Bundle: +1 to combat values (+1 Initiative, +1 to all attacks [ranged and melee], +1 to all damages [ranged and melee]): 3 PP
- Bundle: +1 to combat defenses (+1 to AC, +1 to DR, +1 Soak): 4 PP
- Bundle: +1 Resistance Level to any 3 damage types (e.g., half damage taken from one specific element): 8 PP 
- Bundle: +1 Resistance Level to any 6 damage types (e.g., half damage taken from one specific element): 12 PP
- Bundle: +1 Resistance Level to all damage types (e.g., half damage taken from one specific element): 18 PP
```
bu i wrote them before writing the add new property idea of mine above. i guess, if we do the add new property to the UI we do not have to create these bundles as a new field, right?

also, i made some additions or wording changes:
```
-   +1 Inspiration
-   +1 Soak
-	+1 Pure Hit (adds directly to Attack Resolution)
-	+1 Pure Damage (adds directly to Damage Resolution)
-	+1 Resistance Level to any single damage type (e.g., half damage taken from one specific element): 4 PP

```
and i removed this: `-	Immunity (e.g., total immunity to one specific element or crowd control type): 15 PP ` because 2 x [+1] resistance level means immunity by the game machanics.

let me know if there is or was a misunderstanding for these changes and additions or removal, that needs to be fixed. do not implement any change, let me know, first.

### 278. Assistant

One important exception surfaced from the rules themselves:

- `Artifact` cannot be derived from PP alone.
- Your own rule says it starts in the `1 to 4 PP` band but is still a distinct class with special growth conditions.
- So if we make tier purely auto-derived from PP, `Artifact` disappears as a unique item class.

That is the one place where “PP fully decides tier” is not true in the current rules.

### 279. Assistant

One important exception surfaced from the rules themselves:

- `Artifact` cannot be derived from PP alone.
- Your own rule says it starts in the `1 to 4 PP` band but is still a distinct class with special growth conditions.
- So if we make tier purely auto-derived from PP, `Artifact` disappears as a unique item class.

### 280. Assistant

Yes. There were a few real misunderstandings/gaps.

What is now clear:
- `itemLevel` is unnecessary in the current model.
- `PP` should be the source of truth.
- `qualityTier` should be auto-derived from PP and shown as a greyed-out computed field.
- `base overrides stay free`, per your decision.
- `Pure Hit` / `Pure Damage` are deferred.
- Hybrid custom properties is the right direction, and your bundle list can stay as rules examples only.

What needs to be fixed or made explicit:
- [item_rules_v2.3.txt](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\references\originals\item_rules_v2.3.txt) is still behind your intent.
  - It still contains `Immunity: 15 PP`.
  - It does not yet contain your new `+1 Inspiration`, `+1 Soak`, `+1 Resistance Level to any single damage type: 4 PP`, or the bundle examples.
- The biggest implementation issue is not only bundles.
  - All of `2.4` is currently a problem because utility/major effects are free text today.
  - PP cannot be auto-derived from free text.
  - So special effects need structured custom-property rows with explicit PP cost.
- `Artifact` is the one exception to “PP fully decides tier”.
  - Your rules make it a distinct class that can start in the same PP band as `Uncommon / Masterwork`.
  - So `Artifact` must be a separate flag/class, not a derived tier label.
- Your resistance change is coherent with the current game mechanics.
  - Current resistance levels are `0 = normal`, `1 = half damage`, `2 = immune`.
  - So removing separate `Immunity: 15 PP` and treating immunity as two stacked `+1 resistance level` steps is internally consistent.
  - But it is also a major balance change from the current file.
- One rule area is still underspecified:
  - you added new positive PP entries, but the refund side in section 3 does not yet say whether `-1 Inspiration`, `-1 Soak`, or `-1 Resistance Level` also refund PP.

One more practical consequence:
- [items.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\items.ts) currently uses `itemLevel` mainly for `Artifact Appraisal`.
- Once `itemLevel` is removed, appraisal should gate by derived tier/quality band instead.
- `Artifact` appraisal remains undefined unless you want a separate artifact-identification rule later.

So the direction is sound. The only things that still need explicit rule text are:
- the updated section 2/3/4 values,
- the refund policy for your new categories,
- and the fact that `Artifact` is separate from normal PP-derived tiers.

### 290. Assistant

<proposed_plan>
# PP-Driven Item Quality Refactor

## Summary
- Remove `itemLevel` as a concept from the item system.
- Replace manual `qualityTier` editing with two computed read-only fields:
  - `PP`
  - `Item Tier`
- Treat [item_rules_v2.3.txt](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\references\originals\item_rules_v2.3.txt) as the authority and sync [item_rules.json](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\json_refs\item_rules.json) to it.
- Derive PP from item bonus effects only. Base blueprint values and base overrides remain free.
- Add structured custom-property rows for `2.4` effects so PP can be auto-totaled while still supporting nonstandard bundles and special effects.

## Key Changes
- **Rules and data authority**
  - Update the text rules file to include the bundle examples you listed.
  - Update the JSON mirror to match the saved text file exactly.
  - Make refund math explicitly symmetric with PP cost:
    - anything that costs `+N PP` refunds `-N PP` when applied as a drawback
  - Keep `+1 Pure Hit` and `+1 Pure Damage` in the rules source, but mark them deferred in implementation and exclude them from current UI/runtime PP calculation.

- **Item model**
  - Remove `itemLevel` from item records, editor state, persistence, migration helpers, starter items, and appraisal helpers.
  - Replace manual `qualityTier` storage/editing with derived tier computation from net PP.
  - Add computed `propertyPoints` support at the item layer.
  - Add a per-item special flag/classification for `Artifact`.
    - normal items use PP-derived tier
    - `Artifact` remains a separate special class, not a normal derived tier label
  - Keep current blueprint/base-vs-bonus split.
    - `baseProfile` and `baseOverrides` do not contribute PP
    - `bonusProfile` contributes PP
    - custom property rows contribute PP

- **PP calculation**
  - Auto-calculate PP from structured standard bonuses using section `2` and symmetric refunds from section `3`.
  - Standard auto-counted fields in this pass:
    - max HP, max mana, initiative, inspiration
    - specific skills
    - attack-dice hit, damage-dice damage
    - AC, DR, soak
    - core stats
    - single-damage-type resistance levels
    - selected spell bonuses
    - supernatural power bonuses
  - Deferred from auto-counting:
    - pure hit
    - pure damage
    - generic “+1 success to any roll”
  - Derive tier from final net PP:
    - `0` = `Common`
    - `1-4` = `Uncommon / Masterwork`
    - `5-10` = `Rare`
    - `11-18` = `Epic`
    - `19-30` = `Legendary`
    - `31+` = `Mythical / Celestial / Demonic`
  - If `isArtifact` is true, display `Artifact` as the item class while still computing/storing PP internally.

- **Custom property system**
  - Add `customProperties` to item instances.
  - Each custom row supports:
    - label/name
    - notes/description
    - signed manual PP cost
    - signed configurable value to apply
    - selected target fields via multi-select popover
  - A custom row may target:
    - stats
    - skills
    - derived character-sheet fields
    - resistances
    - power bonuses
    - spell bonuses
  - A custom row may also be notes-only with PP cost and no mechanical targets for utility/major/game-altering effects.
  - Custom row PP is included directly in total PP.
  - Custom row effects are merged into the item’s resolved bonus output so assigned characters receive them mechanically.
  - Your listed bundle examples stay as rule examples, not hardcoded presets in the UI.

- **DM item editor and list**
  - Replace editable `Item Level` and `Quality Tier` inputs in the DM item editor with greyed-out computed fields:
    - `PP`
    - `Item Tier`
  - Add a `Custom Properties` editor section below the standard structured bonus fields.
  - Keep existing standard structured bonus inputs for common fields.
  - Show PP and derived tier in the DM list and item picker summaries.
  - Base edit mode still works as now, but changing base values does not change PP.

- **Artifact Appraisal**
  - Replace level-based item identification with tier-based identification for normal items.
  - Map current Awareness appraisal gates to derived tiers:
    - level 1: `Common`, `Uncommon / Masterwork`
    - level 2: `Rare` or lower
    - level 3: `Epic` or lower
    - level 4: `Legendary` or lower
    - level 5: `Mythical / Celestial / Demonic` or lower
  - `Artifact` appraisal is not auto-resolved in this refactor.
    - default behavior: artifacts are excluded from normal automatic appraisal checks and remain DM/manual identification only for now

## Test Plan
- Migrations:
  - old items with `itemLevel` and manual `qualityTier` hydrate into the new model without data loss
  - starter items migrate cleanly and show `0 PP` / `Common`
- PP calculation:
  - standard positive bonuses add correct PP
  - negative bonuses refund correct PP symmetrically
  - resistances cost `4 PP` per level
  - base blueprint values and base overrides contribute `0 PP`
  - deferred categories do not accidentally affect PP
- Tier derivation:
  - each PP band maps to the correct tier label
  - `Artifact` displays as a special class regardless of normal tier label
- Custom properties:
  - manual PP rows affect total PP
  - targeted rows apply their configured signed value to selected fields
  - notes-only rows affect PP but not sheet stats
- Appraisal:
  - normal items use tier-based appraisal gating
  - artifacts are excluded from automatic appraisal in this pass
- Regression:
  - current item assignment/equipment behavior still works
  - current item bonuses still resolve into character runtime correctly

## Assumptions
- The saved text file is the current authority, and the JSON mirror will be brought into sync during implementation.
- `Pure Hit`, `Pure Damage`, and `+1 success to any roll` remain rule concepts but are explicitly deferred from this implementation pass.
- `Artifact` is modeled as a separate item classification flag, not as a normal PP-derived tier.
- Base blueprint edits and item-only base overrides remain free and do not affect PP.
</proposed_plan>

## My request for Codex:
how do i share it? to a character?

### 365. Assistant

I’m checking the exact assignment flow in the current code so I answer with what actually exists, not what was planned.

### 366. Assistant

I’m checking the exact assignment flow in the current code so I answer with what actually exists, not what was planned.

### 367. Assistant

Yes. In the current implementation, “share to a character” means `assign item to character`.

How:
1. Open `DM Dashboard` -> `Item Management` -> `Items List`
2. Find the item
3. Click the row to expand it
4. Use the `Assigned Character` dropdown
5. Pick the character

What it does:
- sets `assignedCharacterId`
- adds the item to that character’s `owned` and `inventory` references
- removes it from any previously assigned character
- does **not** auto-equip it

So:
- `Item Editting` = edit the item
- `Items List` = assign/share it to a character

If you want, I can also add the same `Assigned Character` control directly into `Item Editting`.

## My request for Codex:
i created a new item and i gave it to a character. the character's sheet shows the item. i can see it in the character's inverntory, but not in loadout. how will i make this character to put this item on?

### 370. Assistant

Current behavior:

- assigning an item only gives it to the character
- it does not equip it automatically
- `inventory` and `loadout` are separate

To put it on:
1. Open that character sheet
2. Go to `Character Gear`
3. In the `Loadout` area, use the slot dropdowns
4. Select the item for the relevant slot

Examples:
- armor -> `Armor` slot
- shield -> `Shield` or a hand/equipment slot depending on your setup
- weapon -> `Primary Hand` / `Secondary Hand`

If the item is only visible under `Items` and not showing as selectable in `Loadout`, then that is a UI/data-link issue and I should inspect the loadout slot source.

### 377. Assistant

You’re missing two things:

1. `Edit mode`
- The screen in the screenshot is read-only.
- You need `Edit Sheet` or `DM Edit: On` first.

2. An `other equipment slot` entry
- The fixed loadout only shows:
  - `Primary Hand`
  - `Secondary Hand`
- Your shield is not auto-placed there.
- Shields currently need a manual extra equipment entry.

What to do:
1. Turn on `Edit Sheet` or `DM Edit: On`
2. Go to `Equipment` -> `Loadout`
3. Click `Add Other Slot`
4. In `Slot`, type `Shield`
5. In the item dropdown, select `Turtle Shield`

Why this happens:
- assignment to character only puts the item in inventory
- equip/loadout is separate
- the current UI has fixed weapon-hand slots, and shields use the editable “other slot” path

So the real missing piece is:
- no `Shield` loadout slot has been created yet

If you want, I can improve this so shields and armor get dedicated built-in loadout slots instead of requiring manual `Add Other Slot`.

## My request for Codex:
`Q`: first, i have a question to you. may i roll back to any rollback commit code/tag or only to the very last commit code/code?

`> How should the daily rollback automation behave?` -> rules for this behaviour:
1. if there is no change/update on codebase from the last rollback point creation, no auto-rollback,
2. if there is a change/update on codebase, check for the last rollback's time/date,
3. if the last rollback's time/date is more than a 18 hours ago, draft a rollback,
4. request a review for the drafted rollback,
5. if you receive a response act accordingly,
6. if the response says later without specifying a specific time/date or event, add another 9 hours to the clock (total 27 hours from the last rollback),
7. if the answer to the question `Q` is "yes, i can roll back to any commit code/tag", then do the following (8):
8. if you do not receive any response, create an auto-rollback.
9. If the answer to the question `Q` is "no, you can only rollback to the last commit", then switch to a new branch (add `1` or (if `1` already exists) change (increase) the number at the end of current branch) and create an auto-rollback.

`> What time should it run each day in your local timezone?` -> i gave you the time specifics above, but if that does not work for you and you need a specific, routine time for each time, you may use 09:00.

### 487. Assistant

Yes. In git, you can roll back to any reachable commit or tag, not only the latest commit.

Important correction:
- a rollback `tag` only points to a commit
- it does not capture uncommitted working-tree changes

So for your automation, if the repo has changes since the last rollback point, an auto-rollback must create a checkpoint commit first, then tag that commit. Otherwise there is nothing new to roll back to.

### 488. Assistant

Important correction:
- a rollback `tag` only points to a commit
- it does not capture uncommitted working-tree changes

So for your automation, if the repo has changes since the last rollback point, an auto-rollback must create a checkpoint commit first, then tag that commit. Otherwise there is nothing new to roll back to.

### 489. Assistant

Yes. Your understanding is correct.

Precise answer to `Q`:
- you can roll back to any reachable commit or tag, not only the latest commit
- but a tag only points to a commit
- so if there are uncommitted changes, the automation must commit first, then tag that commit, otherwise there is no new rollback point to return to

Because of that, your step `9` does not apply here. The automation can stay on the current branch.

### 490. Assistant

Yes. Your understanding is correct.

- you can roll back to any reachable commit or tag, not only the latest commit
- but a tag only points to a commit
- so if there are uncommitted changes, the automation must commit first, then tag that commit, otherwise there is no new rollback point to return to

Because of that, your step `9` does not apply here. The automation can stay on the current branch.

<proposed_plan>
# Daily Rollback Automation

## Summary
- Add one recurring automation for this repo.
- The automation’s job is not a simple reminder; it is a gated rollback-checkpoint workflow.
- A rollback point is defined as:
  - a checkpoint commit, then
  - a rollback tag on that commit
- Because your `18h` and `27h` rules are relative, the automation should run hourly, not once per day. A daily `09:00` run cannot satisfy the `later -> +9h` rule reliably.

## Key Behavior
- Run every hour for this workspace.
- On each run:
  - detect the latest rollback tag in the repo
  - compare current repo state against that rollback point
  - treat both committed changes and uncommitted working-tree changes as “change/update on codebase”
- If there is no change since the last rollback point:
  - do nothing
- If there is change:
  - read the timestamp of the latest rollback point
  - if it is `<= 18h` old, do nothing
  - if it is `> 18h` old and there is no pending review request, open an inbox review request with a drafted rollback plan
- Drafted rollback plan must include:
  - current branch
  - latest rollback tag
  - whether working tree is dirty
  - whether there are commits after the last rollback
  - proposed checkpoint commit message
  - proposed rollback tag name
- If you reply with approval:
  - create the checkpoint commit if needed
  - create the rollback tag
- If you reply `later` with no specific time/date/event:
  - defer until `27h` from the last rollback timestamp
- If there is no response:
  - once the automation reaches the first eligible run after the deadline, auto-create the rollback point
- Since the answer to `Q` is yes:
  - auto-create on the current branch
  - do not create a numbered side branch

## Implementation Details
- Schedule:
  - hourly automation for this repo
  - local timezone: `America/New_York`
- Rollback tag naming:
  - `rollback/auto-YYYY-MM-DD-HHmm`
- Checkpoint commit message:
  - `chore: auto rollback checkpoint YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm`
- “Change/update on codebase” means either:
  - `HEAD` differs from the commit pointed to by the latest rollback tag, or
  - the working tree/index is dirty
- Review/defer state should be stored in the automation’s own memory so the automation can remember:
  - pending review opened at `>18h`
  - whether `later` was received
  - the defer deadline
  - the last proposed tag/commit for that pending checkpoint
- If no rollback tag exists yet:
  - treat the repo as having no prior checkpoint
  - if the repo has changes, open the first review request immediately
- If there are no uncommitted changes but there are committed changes after the last rollback:
  - create only the rollback tag on current `HEAD`
- If there are uncommitted changes:
  - create the checkpoint commit first, then tag it

## Test / Acceptance
- No changes since last rollback:
  - automation opens nothing
- Changes exist, last rollback newer than 18h:
  - automation opens nothing
- Changes exist, last rollback older than 18h:
  - automation opens one review request with drafted checkpoint details
- Reply `later`:
  - automation does not create a rollback before `27h`
- No response:
  - automation auto-creates checkpoint commit if needed, then rollback tag
- Existing committed changes only:
  - automation tags `HEAD` without making an extra commit
- Uncommitted changes:
  - automation creates commit first, then tags it

## Assumptions
- This applies to the current workspace only:
  - `C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5`
- Current branch history may receive checkpoint commits from the automation.
- The repo’s existing phase rollback tags remain untouched; this automation adds separate `rollback/auto-*` tags.
</proposed_plan>

## My request for Codex:
PLEASE IMPLEMENT THIS PLAN:
# Daily Rollback Automation

## Summary
- Add one recurring automation for this repo.
- The automation’s job is not a simple reminder; it is a gated rollback-checkpoint workflow.
- A rollback point is defined as:
  - a checkpoint commit, then
  - a rollback tag on that commit
- Because your `18h` and `27h` rules are relative, the automation should run hourly, not once per day. A daily `09:00` run cannot satisfy the `later -> +9h` rule reliably.

## Key Behavior
- Run every hour for this workspace.
- On each run:
  - detect the latest rollback tag in the repo
  - compare current repo state against that rollback point
  - treat both committed changes and uncommitted working-tree changes as “change/update on codebase”
- If there is no change since the last rollback point:
  - do nothing
- If there is change:
  - read the timestamp of the latest rollback point
  - if it is `<= 18h` old, do nothing
  - if it is `> 18h` old and there is no pending review request, open an inbox review request with a drafted rollback plan
- Drafted rollback plan must include:
  - current branch
  - latest rollback tag
  - whether working tree is dirty
  - whether there are commits after the last rollback
  - proposed checkpoint commit message
  - proposed rollback tag name
- If you reply with approval:
  - create the checkpoint commit if needed
  - create the rollback tag
- If you reply `later` with no specific time/date/event:
  - defer until `27h` from the last rollback timestamp
- If there is no response:
  - once the automation reaches the first eligible run after the deadline, auto-create the rollback point
- Since the answer to `Q` is yes:
  - auto-create on the current branch
  - do not create a numbered side branch

## Implementation Details
- Schedule:
  - hourly automation for this repo
  - local timezone: `America/New_York`
- Rollback tag naming:
  - `rollback/auto-YYYY-MM-DD-HHmm`
- Checkpoint commit message:
  - `chore: auto rollback checkpoint YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm`
- “Change/update on codebase” means either:
  - `HEAD` differs from the commit pointed to by the latest rollback tag, or
  - the working tree/index is dirty
- Review/defer state should be stored in the automation’s own memory so the automation can remember:
  - pending review opened at `>18h`
  - whether `later` was received
  - the defer deadline
  - the last proposed tag/commit for that pending checkpoint
- If no rollback tag exists yet:
  - treat the repo as having no prior checkpoint
  - if the repo has changes, open the first review request immediately
- If there are no uncommitted changes but there are committed changes after the last rollback:
  - create only the rollback tag on current `HEAD`
- If there are uncommitted changes:
  - create the checkpoint commit first, then tag it

## Test / Acceptance
- No changes since last rollback:
  - automation opens nothing
- Changes exist, last rollback newer than 18h:
  - automation opens nothing
- Changes exist, last rollback older than 18h:
  - automation opens one review request with drafted checkpoint details
- Reply `later`:
  - automation does not create a rollback before `27h`
- No response:
  - automation auto-creates checkpoint commit if needed, then rollback tag
- Existing committed changes only:
  - automation tags `HEAD` without making an extra commit
- Uncommitted changes:
  - automation creates commit first, then tags it

## Assumptions
- This applies to the current workspace only:
  - `C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5`
- Current branch history may receive checkpoint commits from the automation.
- The repo’s existing phase rollback tags remain untouched; this automation adds separate `rollback/auto-*` tags.

::automation-update{mode="suggested create" name="Daily rollback checkpoint" prompt="Check this repo for rollback-point freshness. Use the latest git tag matching `rollback/*` as the last rollback point. If the codebase has not changed since that rollback point, do nothing. Treat changes as either commits after that rollback commit or a dirty working tree/index. If there is change and the last rollback point is more than 18 hours old, open an inbox item requesting review of a drafted rollback checkpoint. The draft must include the current branch, latest rollback tag, whether the working tree is dirty, whether commits exist after the last rollback, the proposed checkpoint commit message `chore: auto rollback checkpoint YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm`, and the proposed tag name `rollback/auto-YYYY-MM-DD-HHmm`. Store pending review and defer state in automation memory. If the user replies with approval, create the checkpoint: if the working tree is dirty, commit first on the current branch, then create the rollback tag; if HEAD already contains the changes and the tree is clean, just create the rollback tag on HEAD. If the user replies `later` with no specific time, date, or event, defer action until 27 hours after the last rollback timestamp. If there is no response by the first eligible run after that 27-hour mark, auto-create the rollback point on the current branch. Do not use a numbered side branch. Keep existing phase rollback tags untouched and only add new `rollback/auto-*` tags. Always open an inbox item for review steps or for reporting an auto-created rollback point." rrule="FREQ=HOURLY;INTERVAL=1" cwds="C:\\Users\\Evrim\\Desktop\\FRP\\Convergence\\game_hub5" status="ACTIVE"}

# Repository Instructions

## Execution Workflow
- Treat `references/plan.md` as the authoritative implementation plan.
- Always start with the earliest unfinished plan item.
- Break that item into concrete tasks, complete them one at a time, verify each one, and only then move to the next task.
- Update `references/plan.md` only when implementation reality requires a change.

## Remote Sync
- After completing a substantial plan item such as `0.2`, `0.3`, `1.1`, or `3.2`, create a focused commit and push it to `origin` so the remote repository reflects major progress checkpoints.

## Phase Checkpoints
- When an entire phase is complete, create a clearly named GitHub checkpoint for that phase so there is a stable recovery marker for later reference.
- Prefer a GitHub milestone for tracking visibility, and use a git-native checkpoint such as a tag or equivalent marker when an actual rollback point is required.
- Use rollback tags in the format `rollback/phase-<n>-<short-name>` so phase checkpoints are easy to identify and reuse.

</INSTRUCTIONS>

### 527. Assistant

Yes. Comparing against `673f553` is the right move.

What I found already:
- The regression is concentrated in persistence/state, not the visible power UI.
- Since `673f553`, the biggest risky change is:
  - [src/state/appFlowPersistence.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\state\appFlowPersistence.ts)
  - plus its wiring in [src/state/appFlow.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\state\appFlow.tsx)
- The storage model changed from roughly:
  - `characters + items`
- to:
  - `characters + itemBlueprints + itemInstances + starterItemsInitialized`

Why that matters:
- It matches your symptoms exactly.
- Starter blueprints/items still exist because the new code reseeds them.
- A custom item like `Turtle Shield` can disappear if it is filtered out during hydration.
- Character visibility can break if persisted state is read/written in the wrong shape.
- The power-assignment problem is probably secondary fallout from bad hydrated character state, not from [CharacterPowersSection.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterPowersSection.tsx), which only changed rendering.

On the rollback automation:
- If daily at `07:07` is acceptable to you, then yes, it is operational enough.
- One caveat: it is pinned to branch `codex/powers-implementation`. It will not automatically follow future branches.

My recommendation:
1. Treat `673f553` as the known-good baseline.
2. Repair the persistence layer first:
   - [src/state/appFlowPersistence.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\state\appFlowPersistence.ts)
   - [src/state/appFlow.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\state\appFlow.tsx)
3. Do not start with character-sheet UI or power UI.
4. After persistence is stable, recheck:
   - existing saved characters
   - new character creation
   - adding powers
   - custom item survival across reload
   - equip/unequip without edit mode

So: I agree with your approach, and the likely culprit is the new persistence migration around blueprints/item instances, not the earlier stable character-sheet code. If you want, I’ll start the repair from those two files first.

### 530. Assistant

**Fix Plan**

Goal:
- keep all current item/blueprint/PP/custom-property functionality
- do not revert code
- use `673f553` only as a reference baseline for expected character behavior

**Working assumption**
- the regression source is the persistence/migration layer introduced with:
  - [C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\state\appFlowPersistence.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\state\appFlowPersistence.ts)
  - [C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\state\appFlow.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\state\appFlow.tsx)

**Plan**
1. Define the pre-regression behavior contract from `673f553`
- compare only these flows:
  - saved characters remain visible after reload
  - new characters can be created
  - powers can be added to new characters
  - shared items persist across reload
- use the old checkpoint as an oracle, not as rollback input

2. Audit the current storage schema end to end
- inspect serialized shape now written to local storage
- verify read/write symmetry for:
  - `characters`
  - `itemBlueprints`
  - `itemInstances`
  - legacy `items`
  - `starterItemsInitialized`
- identify where valid saved entries are being dropped during hydration

3. Repair hydration without removing new features

### 574. Assistant

Not before. I just checked as far as I can from the filesystem.

What I can say now:
- An open browser does **not** mean the old characters should still be there.
- If the tab already refreshed into the bad empty state, that empty state may already have been written back to `localStorage` while the browser stayed open.
- So “browser still open” only helps if:
  - another tab still has the old in-memory state and has not reloaded, or
  - the `localStorage` key was never overwritten.

Given what you showed earlier:
- the app was already rendering an empty roster on `localhost:5173`
- that makes it likely the bad/empty state had already become the active saved state on that origin

I did a basic storage check:
- I confirmed the browser storage directories exist
- I could **not** confirm an intact old `convergence.local.characters` payload from disk alone
- Chrome stores this in LevelDB, so it is not straightforward plain-text recovery

So the direct answer is:
- no, the fact that the browser stayed open does not by itself mean the old characters should still be there

If you want the next step, I can help you check the live `localStorage` value directly from the browser console, which is the fastest definitive check.

### 585. Assistant

I’ve isolated the cause. I’m running a quick validation on the patch so I can tell you whether the loop is actually closed.

### 586. Assistant

Cause:
- the DM item editor had a create-on-load effect for `?create=1`
- that effect could re-run before the URL was fully normalized to `?itemId=...`
- each re-run created another item
- that is why you saw the `itemId` keep changing and many new items appearing

I patched it in:
- [C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\routes\DmItemEditPage.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\routes\DmItemEditPage.tsx)

What changed:
- the create request is now handled only once per `?create=1`
- the URL is replaced immediately with `?itemId=...`

Validation:
- `npm.cmd run typecheck`
- `npm.cmd run build`

Both passed.

What you should do now:
- refresh the page once
- the endless creation should stop

What remains:
- the extra items that were already created will still be there
- I can clean those up next, but I should do it carefully so I do not delete a real item you want to keep

## My request for Codex:
i created a shield and equiped it to a char. problem: it is a shield, shield is a hand slot item (secondary hand - precisely), see attached, how it looks.

<image>
</image>

### 602. Assistant

Yes. That is a modeling bug.

Current code treats shields as:
- non-weapon equipment
- separate `Shield` slot

But your rule is:
- shield is a hand-slot item
- specifically secondary hand

That means the current behavior is wrong.

Correct behavior should be:
- equipping a shield places it in `Secondary Hand`
- not in a separate `Shield` slot
- it should compete with off-hand weapon use
- a two-handed weapon should block shield equip
- a shield should block off-hand weapon equip

Recommended fix:
1. Remove the special non-weapon `Shield` slot behavior.
2. Treat shield blueprints as hand-slot equipment in character loadout logic.
3. Default auto-equip for shields to `weapon_secondary`.
4. If `Primary Hand` has a two-handed weapon, prevent shield equip.
5. If a shield is equipped, `Secondary Hand` cannot hold another weapon/item at the same time.

I should implement that in:
- [C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\hooks\usePlayerCharacterMutations.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\hooks\usePlayerCharacterMutations.ts)
- [C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\mutations\characterItemMutations.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterInventorySection.tsx)
- possibly small display cleanup in [C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterInventorySection.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterInventorySection.tsx)

No question needed. I can patch that next.

## My request for Codex:
if there is a mis understanding about Lunar Bless, i'd like to fix that. it si an aura spell and it is active at all times. `Nightvision: Self + 4` any number given after `+` is indicating an additional ally. so the caster (self) will have it at L1 and each level after that it can provide nightvision to an additional ally. if that is creating confusion, let's fix that by changing the wording with `self + 1 ally`, `self + 2 ally` so and so forth. but of course, we need to reflect that to the spells as well. i suppose the question will be what will happen with the mana bonus. if it would simplify things, i can offer, something like this:
```
Level 1. Mana Bonus: +1, Night Vision.
Target: Self 

Level 2. Mana Bonus: +2, Night Vision.
Target: Self  + 1 ally

Level 3. Mana Bonus: +3, Night Vision.
Target: Self + 2  ally

Level 4. Mana Bonus: +4, Night Vision.
Target: Self  + 3  ally

Level 5. Mana Bonus: +5, Night Vision.
Target: Self  + 4 ally
```

what do you say?

### 627. Assistant

Yes. That wording is better.

Current ambiguity:
- `Night Vision: Self + 4` can be read as:
  - a numeric bonus, or
  - self plus four targets
- that is a bad rules sentence for implementation

Your rewritten version is clearer because it separates:
- effect
- target count

Recommended final wording:
```txt
Level 1. Mana Bonus: +1, Night Vision.
Target: Self

Level 2. Mana Bonus: +2, Night Vision.
Target: Self + 1 ally

Level 3. Mana Bonus: +3, Night Vision.
Target: Self + 2 allies

Level 4. Mana Bonus: +4, Night Vision.
Target: Self + 3 allies

Level 5. Mana Bonus: +5, Night Vision.
Target: Self + 4 allies
```

Two small fixes:
- use `allies`, not `ally`, for levels 3-5
- keep the target line separate from the mana bonus/effect line

Design interpretation:
- `Mana Bonus` remains caster-only unless you explicitly want it shared
- `Night Vision` is the shareable aura effect
- that is the cleanest and easiest runtime model

So my recommendation is:
- adopt this wording
- interpret Lunar Bless as:
  - caster always gets mana bonus
  - caster always gets night vision
  - higher levels expand how many allies can also receive night vision

If you want, I can next update the source text and then align the runtime/spell metadata to that wording.

# Repository Instructions

## Execution Workflow
- Treat `references/plan.md` as the authoritative implementation plan.
- Always start with the earliest unfinished plan item.
- Break that item into concrete tasks, complete them one at a time, verify each one, and only then move to the next task.
- Update `references/plan.md` only when implementation reality requires a change.

## Remote Sync
- After completing a substantial plan item such as `0.2`, `0.3`, `1.1`, or `3.2`, create a focused commit and push it to `origin` so the remote repository reflects major progress checkpoints.

## Phase Checkpoints
- When an entire phase is complete, create a clearly named GitHub checkpoint for that phase so there is a stable recovery marker for later reference.
- Prefer a GitHub milestone for tracking visibility, and use a git-native checkpoint such as a tag or equivalent marker when an actual rollback point is required.
- Use rollback tags in the format `rollback/phase-<n>-<short-name>` so phase checkpoints are easy to identify and reuse.

### 634. Assistant

Yes. I would reflect it like this:

```text
Level 1. Mana Bonus: +1
Effect: Night Vision
Target: Self

Level 2. Mana Bonus: +2
Effect: Night Vision
Target: Self + 1 ally

Level 3. Mana Bonus: +3
Effect: Night Vision
Target: Self + 2 allies

Level 4. Mana Bonus: +4
Effect: Night Vision
Target: Self + 3 allies

Level 5. Mana Bonus: +5
Effect: Night Vision
Target: Self + 4 allies
```

This is cleaner because:
- `Mana Bonus` is one effect line
- `Night Vision` is the aura effect
- `Target` is isolated, so `Self + N allies` cannot be misread as part of mana scaling

One thing to flag:
- your current text says `Level 3 ... Self + 3`
- if your intent is “each level adds one more ally,” then `Level 3` should be `Self + 2 allies`

If you want, I can next print the exact revised block for `Lunar Bless` in full document style.

PP 20 | Legendary | Slot: Hand | Base: DR +2 | Bonus: Fire/Cold/Acid RL +2

### 694. Assistant

### 695. Assistant

I’m checking the slot definitions and the loadout renderer so I can answer from the current code instead of guessing.

### 696. Assistant

Because the current code only defines two fixed loadout slots: `weapon_primary` and `weapon_secondary`.

Where that comes from:
- Fixed hand-slot ids are declared in [items.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/types/items.ts#L167)
- Their labels are only `Primary Hand` and `Secondary Hand` in [items.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/types/items.ts#L170)
- The character sheet renders loadout by mapping only those two ids in [CharacterInventorySection.tsx](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/components/player-character/CharacterInventorySection.tsx#L137)
- Non-hand equipment is treated as generic “other equipment entries” instead of fixed canonical slots in [items.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/lib/items.ts#L1561)

So the current model is:
- fixed slots: `Primary Hand`, `Secondary Hand`
- everything else: ad hoc equipment entries like `Armor`, `Focus`, `Accessory` if they exist

That means this is not a rules limitation. It is a current UI/data-model limitation.

In practical terms:
- shield is correctly using `Secondary Hand`
- armor/focus/accessories are not yet first-class fixed loadout slots
- that is why you only see two rows by default

Also, `No loadout equipped.` is a little misleading under this model, because it really means:
- no hand-slot items equipped, and
- no dynamic extra equipment entries present

If you want, the correct next fix is to promote non-hand gear into explicit fixed loadout slots, for example:
- `Primary Hand`
- `Secondary Hand`
- `Chest Armor`
- `Focus`
- `Accessory`

I would recommend that over keeping the current mixed fixed/dynamic approach.

## My request for Codex:
`The confusing Inactive state text was removed from the player inventory state line. ` what was it though?

### 699. Assistant

It was this part of the item state line:

```text
Owned | Carried | Inactive
```

That came from the old player inventory state summary, which always printed three flags:
- `Owned`
- `Carried`
- `Active` or `Inactive`

In code, it was generated by `getItemStateSummary(...)` in [CharacterInventorySection.tsx](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/components/player-character/CharacterInventorySection.tsx). Before I changed it, that helper produced:

```ts
[
  ownedItemIds.includes(itemId) ? "Owned" : "Not owned",
  inventoryItemIds.includes(itemId) ? "Carried" : "Not carried",
  activeItemIds.includes(itemId) ? "Active" : "Inactive",
].join(" | ")
```

Why I called it confusing:
- in the current item/equipment flow, “active” is not the same thing as “equipped”
- so an equipped shield could still show `Inactive`, which reads like “not in use” even though it is being worn/held
- for the player-facing inventory row, that was more misleading than helpful

So I removed that third status from the player read-only inventory line. Now it only reflects the inventory-style state, not the separate active-state mechanic.

## My request for Codex:
what do you mean by unknown extra slots?

### 731. Assistant

I mean any equipment entry whose `slot` string is not one of the 7 canonical slots and also not one of the old legacy names I explicitly mapped.

Canonical slots now are:
- `weapon_primary`
- `weapon_secondary`
- `ring_left`
- `ring_right`
- `body`
- `neck`
- `head`

Legacy names I explicitly map into those are things like:
- `Primary Hand`
- `Secondary Hand`
- `Shield`
- `Armor`
- `Focus`
- `Accessory`
- `Chest`
- `Left Ring`
- `Right Ring`

So “unknown extra slots” would be entries like:
- `Belt`
- `Cape`
- `Relic`
- `Pet Slot`
- `Trinket A`
- any custom/free-typed slot name that already exists in saved data

What happens to those:
- I do not delete them
- I do not force-map them into one of the 7 main slots
- they remain as extra equipment entries and still render below the main slots

That was deliberate, to avoid destroying or silently misplacing existing saved equipment data.

So:
- known legacy slot names get normalized into the new 7-slot model
- truly unknown/custom slot names are preserved as extras until we explicitly decide how they should behave

### 733. User

# Context from my IDE setup:

## Active file: references/originals/T1 Supernatural Powers_v1.1.txt

## Open tabs:
- T1 Supernatural Powers_v1.1.txt: references/originals/T1 Supernatural Powers_v1.1.txt
- item_rules_v2.3.txt: references/originals/item_rules_v2.3.txt
- resistance_rules.json: json_refs/resistance_rules.json
- power_spell_ingestion_normalized_current.json: references/power_spell_ingestion_normalized_current.json
- power_spell_ingestion_decisions_current.json: references/power_spell_ingestion_decisions_current.json
## My request for Codex:
- what are those unknown extra slots?
- under category (in blueprints), there are 4 options: weapon, armor, jewel, mystic.
these categories, should relate to the equipment slots. at least that's what i think, whay would you say?
- matching categories to these 7 slots and then using the subtypes to map into the all other items ... could that be solution to the issue of uknown extra slots?

### 734. Assistant

`Unknown extra slots` means any equipment slot string that is not one of the 7 canonical slots.

Right now, those usually come from older or freer data such as:
- legacy slot names like `Armor`, `Focus`, `Accessory`, `Shield`
- ad hoc custom slots typed through the older `Add Other Slot` path
- typos or one-off labels like `Helmet`, `Body Armor`, `Main Hand`, etc.

I preserved those during normalization because deleting or collapsing them automatically could lose data. So they are not a design goal. They are a compatibility bucket.

On your second point: yes, categories should relate to equipment slots. I agree with that direction.

But I would make one distinction:
- category should define the broad slot family
- subtype should define the exact slot behavior

So category alone is not enough.

Examples:
- `weapon`
  - subtype decides whether it can go in `primary`, `secondary`, or both
  - shield is not `weapon`, but hand-slot behavior is similar
- `armor`
  - `shield_light`, `shield_heavy` -> `secondary hand`
  - `clothing`, `light`, `medium`, `heavy` -> `body`
  - future helmet subtype would go to `head`
- `jewel`
  - generic `jewel` is too vague long-term
  - future subtypes should probably become `ring`, `necklace`, `earring`, `charm/talisman`
- `mystic`
  - current `focus` can map to `neck`
  - future mystic subtypes could support `orbital`

So to your third point: yes, that is basically the correct solution.

The cleaner model is:
1. closed slot system
   - only the 7 main slots now
   - later 3 supplementary slots when DM unlocks them
2. blueprint-driven slot rules
   - each blueprint should resolve to an allowed slot set and a default slot
3. category + subtype determine slot mapping
   - not free-text slot names
4. legacy unknown slots are only migration leftovers
   - not something new data should keep producing

That would solve the `unknown extra slots` issue going forward.

My recommendation:
- keep `unknown extra slots` only as legacy compatibility during hydration
- stop generating new arbitrary slot names in normal flows
- eventually remove or restrict the free-form `Add Other Slot` path
- move slot authority into blueprint logic

In short:
- yes, your idea is correct
- but the real authority should be `category + subtype -> allowed/default slots`
- not category alone

If you want, the next implementation step should be:
- formalize a slot-mapping table for the current blueprint set
- prevent new non-canonical slot creation in normal character-sheet flows
- keep legacy extra slots readable only for backward compatibility
